The brushes in this quality category are specifically: the F71 XL fan brush (made of sable hair), the F19 slanted contour brush, the F14 medium powder brush, the F13 rounded foundation brush (excellent!), M33 mineral powder brush, F17 buffed bronzer brush (goat hair) and M22 mineral bronze buffer brush. The regular foundation brush is ok too, but not so dense. Also, all the eye brushes are outstanding - though I use the one labelled \\"E11 eyeshadow brush\\" for concealer and the \\"F70 concealer brush\\" for eyeshadow instead (both good). If you take care of them, they should last for years. Very soft, but good density overall for these brushes. A comparable set to these are the coastal scents 22-piece brush set, but this one's way better. If you're on the fence between that one and this, get this for sure. This one is what I wished the coastal scents was going to be (I was very disappointed by the 22 piece set, that everyone seemed to rave about). Now onto the bad, or at least the \\"not so good\\": some of the brushes shed - I'm disappointed for example with the duo-fibre brushes (F10 oval liquid foundation brush, and F12 liquid foundation buffer brush). These ones are duo-fibre synthetic and sable hair, and the F10 can't stop shedding it seems. Very sad - because I wanted a brush like this one and I don't seem to have any luck with these kind of brushes. The equivalent brush in the 22 piece coastal scents kit was also very disappointing for the lack of bristle density, so I was hoping this one would be a great replacement, but no such luck - if it keeps shedding, it'll also lose density. Also the goat hair F17 buffed bronzer brush shed a bit, but it seems more manageable than the F10 or F12. Additionally, the medium powder brush (F14) hasn't been finished properly - it lacks the crimps on the ferrule (metal part of the brush) that would normally secure it to the wooden handle. I noticed one other customer complained that two of her brushes came apart within a short time, so I really hope that doesn't happen to this one, or any of mine. And although the brush roll is great overall, it seems a part of it also hasn't been finished properly - the seam for the F12 brush pouch doesn't go all the way up to the top of the pouch as the others do. If I could fix it, I would, but one would need an industrial sewing machine to fix it, which I don't have. Some of the other brushes such as the M21 slanted mineral blush brush, F22 slanted finishing brush and E25 slanted eyeliner brush also seem to have minor defects. The M21 and F22 seem not to have been trimmed properly and both have a slight to moderate concave dips within the centre where it should be straight across in a diagonal cut. And the E25 seems to have the bottom part of the bristles on one side, kind of \\"dented\\" if that makes any sense. It basically looks like whatever was used to trim this brush (laser or whatever) was first accidentally aimed at the bottom part of the brush. But so far it seems to work fine, so perhaps it's just a cosmetic issue. I think if you're in the US, you should get this set directly from the Shany website, because there they're selling it for only $30.00, and not $69.95, which is what I see today here on amazon. It's overall quite good, if you want better quality than E.L.F. or other drugstore brands. But do be aware that there seems to be somequality control issues - from reading other reviews, it seems other customers have had similar, but not the exact same issues relating to the finishing of the brushes and case. Finally to address the claim that Shany is cruelty free - that very well may be true as far as the makeup is concerned, but if you really care about cruelty free makeup brushes - get synthetic taklon brushes such as ecotools and real techniques. That's the only way to be sure. I have both these brands and they are excellent, and especially real techniques is as close to pro quality as you'll get given the price. Take it with a grain of salt when a business claims they have cruelty-free natural animal hair brushes in the mix. This brush set is made in China after all.

  105. I wanted to wait until I used these & washed them several times before writing my review. Before deciding to finally purchase these, I did extensive research on them and compared them with many other sets offered on Amazon. I like to get the absolute most for my money &, as a former teacher, I like to share what I've learned.<br /><br /> As I researched I learned that the highest quality brushes are handcrafted and made of natural hair. Natural hair is good for applying powders as they distribute the powder more evenly, Synthetic bristles are non-porous and don't absorb as much liquid or cream as the natural bristles, thus not wasting product. Because they are non-porous, they are also easier to wash & some say more hygienic. The bristles should be laser- cut for easy/even application,The ferrules (metal attached to the handle & bristles) should be well-crimped two or three times to be sure the bristles are firmly attached to the handle. The handle should be solid wood with a good weight and easy to hold. I also found a website (sorry I can't find that link anymore) that listed the 10 best inexpensive brush sets to buy and this set was at the top with the Coastal Scents 22 piece set. I can't remember which was first and second, but I think this may have been the set that came in 2nd. The Coastal Scents brushes did not list a lot of information and, personally, these look so much more luxurious compared to the Coastal Scents set. It's very well worth the extra few dollars and you get 2 extra brushes. I also like the variety of the brushes offered in the Shany set better.<br /><br />These Shany brushes are just one of the few I found on Amazon with all of those attributes, and the ONLY ones that have been through a process that treats the brushes and makes them all anti-bacterial. On top of that they had great reviews and are a great price! (This set is $70 or more on other websites) If you'd rather not spend $40 on this set, even Shany's less expensive brushes have most of the same attributes. Another great &#34;extra&#34; is a detailed picture with a number and description of each brush in the set, and each brush is also labeled with that number and description. Many brush sets make you guess which brush does what. Even better, they are shipped by Amazon and come with the Amazon guarantee, and member of PETA so they don't harm animals.<br /><br />Now my personal experience with these brushes. They arrived within 3-4 days of ordering and in perfect condition. Not one of the handles was broken or loose. They came enclosed in a very sturdy cardboard box that is perfect to wrap if giving as a gift. The black brush case was enclosed inside the box with each brush wrapped in cellophane. The larger brushes also came with nice,sturdy plastic brush protectors.<br /><br />The case: Is very well made of thick, black faux leather material with wrap around strings that reach around, more than enough, to tie it closed. The individual brush compartments in mine were sewn a bit crooked, but the brushes are held in place just right. It has four extra slots that are not as expanded as the other slots, but I am able to fit two thin brushes in each (eyeliner/lip/spoolie). There is one open mesh pocket and a zippered. mesh pocket on each side of the case that can store small items like brush guards, thin sponges, small tubes.<br /><br />The brushes: They are so soft and well made! I had only minimal shedding from one or two of the brushes when I washed them before use. One was the fan brush and another was one of the Kabuki brushes F-10 or F-12. which are the only brushes in the set I don't like because my foundation came out streaky. I'm not a cosmetologist so I may not have used the proper technique. However, I will probably try them again. All the rest of the brushes have worked beautifully for me. They have washed well without too much effort. I've had no chipping paint or wood, and do additional shedding. They do call the brush & comb brush a &#34;spoolie&#34;, but you will notice in the photo there isn't a true spoolie. I took one from another set to put in one of the extra slots as well as lip liner brush, lipstick brush, and a very thin eyeliner brush. I have t o say that the eye brushes are absolutely phenomenal! There are 9 of them. Those and the fan brush are my favorites.<br /><br />Helpful hints: I didn't pay attention to what order the brushes arrrived in and there are so may all I could remember was the fan brush went in the middle. One thing I wish they would have done to make it easier to find the brushes on the chart, is to have the brushes in the same order they are on the photo description paper that was included. I found a way, though, to organize the brushes the best of my ability so I learn where they are without having to look at the paper all the time to find what I need. I'm a homemaker now, so I don't wear makeup as much as I used to, so it's going to take a few more times for me to get it down pat. The instructions don't mention this, but I noticed a correlation between the letters and what each brush was used for:<br /><br />F- all of these brushes have to deal with the face (11 brushes) All of these are large, except the concealer brush.<br />E- these brushes are for the eyes (8 brushes) These are all small.<br />M- Mineral (powders, bronzer, blush) 3 brushes- large<br />B- Brows (2 brushes)-small<br /><br />The only exception is the blending brush that I use for shadow has the letter F, but I guess it could also be used for the face, too.<br />I grouped them together by letter and numerical sequence as best as I could.<br /><br />I put all the eye shadow brushes & blending brush in the small slots on the left side, The concealer, eyeliner & brow brushes I put in the last slots on the right. The fan brush is exactly in the middle and slightly falls between the folds of the case. I haven't had trouble with the bristles being bent, but the outer plastic brush guard does fold over on each side. I tried the fan brush in a different spot, but it just didn't look right, so I just deal with it because the brush isn't being damaged. I keep the extra flat slots on each side of it open so there us plenty of room beside it. The rest of the larger brushes are spread out on the left and the right of the fan brush. I was able to group the 3 &#34;M&#34; brushes together on the left of the fan brush and put F10 & F12 the furthest to the left with mesh brush guards on them to remind me I don't like those ones.<br /><br />I took a photo of the order in which I arranged the brushes , along with their descriptions, to help me find them much easier than the chart they came with.<br /><br />I hope this helps you in making your decision, & if you choose to buy these, I hope you love them as much as I do, :). They do call the brush & comb brush a &#34;spoolie&#34;, but you will notice in the photo there isn't a true spoolie. I took one from another set to put in one of the extra slots as well as lip liner brush, lipstick brush, and a very thin eyeliner brush. I have t o say that the eye brushes are absolutely phenomenal! There are 9 of them. Those and the fan brush are my favorites.<br /><br />Helpful hints: I didn't pay attention to what order the brushes arrrived in and there are so may all I could remember was the fan brush went in the middle. One thing I wish they would have done to make it easier to find the brushes on the chart, is to have the brushes in the same order they are on the photo description paper that was included. I found a way, though, to organize the brushes the best of my ability so I learn where they are without having to look at the paper all the time to find what I need. I'm a homemaker now, so I don't wear makeup as much as I used to, so it's going to take a few more times for me to get it down pat. The instructions don't mention this, but I noticed a correlation between the letters and what each brush was used for:<br /><br />F- all of these brushes have to deal with the face (11 brushes) All of these are large, except the concealer brush.<br />E- these brushes are for the eyes (8 brushes) These are all small.<br />M- Mineral (powders, bronzer, blush) 3 brushes- large<br />B- Brows (2 brushes)-small<br /><br />The only exception is the blending brush that I use for shadow has the letter F, but I guess it could also be used for the face, too.<br />I grouped them together by letter and numerical sequence as best as I could.<br /><br />I put all the eye shadow brushes & blending brush in the small slots on the left side, The concealer, eyeliner & brow brushes I put in the last slots on the right. The fan brush is exactly in the middle and slightly falls between the folds of the case. I haven't had trouble with the bristles being bent, but the outer plastic brush guard does fold over on each side. I tried the fan brush in a different spot, but it just didn't look right, so I just deal with it because the brush isn't being damaged. I keep the extra flat slots on each side of it open so there us plenty of room beside it. The rest of the larger brushes are spread out on the left and the right of the fan brush. I was able to group the 3 &#34;M&#34; brushes together on the left of the fan brush and put F10 & F12 the furthest to the left with mesh brush guards on them to remind me I don't like those ones.<br /><br />I took a photo of the order in which I arranged the brushes , along with their descriptions, to help me find them much easier than the chart they came with.<br /><br />I hope this helps you in making your decision, & if you choose to buy these, I hope you love them as much as I do, :)
